# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes API Server Admission Webhook Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission webhook chain: the webhook admission controller, the webhook call dispatch, and the admission response aggregation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

60-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully found and documented all the Go source files implementing the Kubernetes API server admission webhook chain. Here's a summary of what I discovered:

## Key Findings

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive information about the API server admission webhook chain, organized into four parts:

### 1. **Main Files** (14 core files)
The webhook chain is implemented across two main plugin directories and supporting utilities:
- **Mutating Webhook**: plugin.go, dispatcher.go with patch application
- **Validating Webhook**: plugin.go, dispatcher.go with parallel execution
- **Generic Base**: webhook.go, interfaces.go for shared functionality
- **Request/Response**: admissionreview.go for AdmissionReview object handling
- **Supporting**: accessors, error handlers, configuration managers, initializers

### 2. **Call Chain**
The execution flow:
1. API server calls `Admit()` or `Validate()` on the plugin
2. Plugin delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch()`
3. `ShouldCallHook()` filters webhooks by namespace/object/rules/match conditions
4. Dispatcher calls webhooks in series (mutating) or parallel (validating)
5. `CreateAdmissionObjects()` creates AdmissionReview requests
6. REST client invokes the webhook
7. `VerifyAdmissionResponse()` validates responses
8. Patches are applied (mutating) or rejections are returned

### 3. **Key Components**
- **Dispatcher pattern**: Generic interface with specific implementations for mutating vs validating
- **Response aggregation**: Mutating webhooks apply patches sequentially; validating webhooks aggregate parallel responses
- **Reinvocation**: Mutating webhooks support reinvocation when mutations occur
- **Audit annotations**: Track all webhook mutations and rejections
- **Match conditions**: CEL-based filter
... (truncated)

   }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes API server admission webhook chain is implemented across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. The chain consists of three main components: the webhook admission controller, the webhook call dispatch mechanism, and the admission response aggregation.\\n\\n## Webhook Admission Controllers\\n\\nThe entry points for the admission webhook chain are the MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook plugins:\\n\\n1. **MutatingAdmissionWebhook Plugin** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go`): This plugin implements the `admission.MutationInterface`. The `Admit()` method is called by the API server to apply mutations to incoming requests. It delegates to the generic webhook's `Dispatch()` method.\\n\\n2. **ValidatingAdmissionWebhook Plugin** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go`): This plugin implements the `admission.ValidationInterface`. The `Validate()` method is called by the API server to validate incoming requests. It also delegates to the generic webhook's `Dispatch()` method.\\n\\n## Webhook Call Dispatch\\n\\nThe dispatch mechanism is implemented in the generic webhook and specific dispatcher implementations:\\n\\n1. **Generic Webhook** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/webhook.go`): This is the core controller that manages the entire webhook lifecycle. The `Dispatch()` method orchestrates the process: it checks if the request should call webhooks, retrieves the list of active webhooks from the hook source (configuration manager), and then delegates to the dispatcher.\\n\\n   Key methods:\\n   - `Dispatch()`: Entry point for both mutating and validating webhooks\\n   - `ShouldCallHook()`: Determines if a webhook should be called based on namespace selectors, object selectors, rules, and match conditions\\n\\n2. **Generic Webhook Interfaces** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/interfaces.go`): Defines the `Dispatcher` interface that both mutating and validating dispatchers implement.\\n\\n3. **Mutating Webhook Dispatcher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go`): Implements sequential webhook dispatch for mutating webhooks. Key features:\\n   - Loops through hooks sequentially\\n   - Calls `callAttrMutatingHook()` for each webhook\\n   - Handles patch application and reinvocation\\n   - Supports reinvocation policy for webhooks marked as eligible\\n   - Manages audit annotations for mutations and patches\\n\\n4. **Validating Webhook Dispatcher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go`): Implements parallel webhook dispatch for validating webhooks:\\n   - Pre-filters relevant webhooks based on matching rules\\n   - Spawns goroutines for parallel webhook calls using `callHook()`\\n   - Aggregates errors from all webhook calls\\n   - Returns the first error encountered\\n\\n## Admission Response Aggregation\\n\\nThe response handling and aggregation is implemented in multiple places:\\n\\n1. **AdmissionReview Request/Response Handling** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/request/admissionreview.go`):\\n   - `CreateAdmissionObjects()`: Creates AdmissionReview request objects in both v1 and v1beta1 formats\\n   - `CreateV1AdmissionReview()` and `CreateV1beta1AdmissionReview()`: Construct properly formatted admission requests\\n   - `VerifyAdmissionResponse()`: Validates webhook responses, extracts audit annotations, warnings, patches, and status information\\n\\n2. **Mutating Webhook Dispatcher Response Handling**: The `callAttrMutatingHook()` method in mutating/dispatcher.go:\\n   - Calls the webhook via REST client\\n   - Verifies the admission response using `VerifyAdmissionResponse()`\\n   - Applies JSON patches to the object\\n   - Adds audit annotations for mutations and patches\\n   - Returns rejection status if webhook denies the request\\n\\n3. **Validating Webhook Dispatcher Response Handling**: The `callHook()` method in validating/dispatcher.go:\\n   - Calls the webhook via REST client\\n   - Verifies the admission response\\n   - Extracts audit annotations and warnings\\n   - Returns rejection error if webhook denies the request\\n   - Parallel calls are aggregated with the first error being returned\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n\\n1. **WebhookAccessor** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/accessors.go`): Provides a unified interface for accessing mutating and validating webhook configurations. Implements caching for compiled matchers and REST clients.\\n\\n2. **Error Handling** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/errors/statuserror.go`): The `ToStatusErr()` function converts webhook rejections to proper Kubernetes status errors.\\n\\n3. **Configuration Managers**:\\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/mutating_webhook_manager.go`: Manages MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects\\n   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/validating_webhook_manager.go`: Manages ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects\\n\\n4. **Initializer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/initializer/initializer.go`): Initializes webhook plugins with necessary dependencies.\\n\\n5. **Match Conditions** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/matchconditions/matcher.go`): Handles CEL-based match conditions for webhook invocation filtering.\\n\\n6. **Reinvocation Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/reinvocationcontext.go`): Manages webhook reinvocation for mutating webhooks when mutations change the request object.\\n\\n## Call Flow Summary\\n\\n1. API server calls `Admit()` (mutating) or `Validate()` (validating) on the plugin\\n2. Plugin delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch()`\\n3. `Dispatch()` checks if webhooks should be called and retrieves the webhook list\\n4. Dispatcher's `Dispatch()` is called with the hook list\\n5. For each matching hook, the dispatcher calls the webhook via REST client\\n6. `CreateAdmissionObjects()` creates the AdmissionReview request\\n7. Webhook response is verified with `VerifyAdmissionResponse()`\\n8. For mutating webhooks: patches are applied and mutations are tracked\\n9. For validating webhooks: multiple calls are made in parallel and errors are aggregated\\n10. Final decision and audit annotations are returned to the API server\"\n}\n",
